title="+357">+357</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Sovereign Base Areas of Akrotiri and Dhekelia</b><sup id="cite_ref-BNA1981_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNA1981-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (<abbr title="abbreviated">abbr.</abbr> <b>SBA</b>; <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\xa0\xce\xb5\xcf\x81\xce\xb9\xce\xbf\xcf\x87\xce\xad\xcf\x82 \xce\x9a\xcf\x85\xcf\x81\xce\xaf\xce\xb1\xcf\x81\xcf\x87\xcf\x89\xce\xbd \xce\x92\xce\xac\xcf\x83\xce\xb5\xcf\x89\xce\xbd \xce\x91\xce\xba\xcf\x81\xcf\x89\xcf\x84\xce\xb7\xcf\x81\xce\xaf\xce\xbf\xcf\x85 \xce\xba\xce\xb1\xce\xb9 \xce\x94\xce\xb5\xce\xba\xce\xad\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\xce\xb1\xcf\x82</span>, <i>Perioch\xc3\xa9s Kyr\xc3\xadarchon V\xc3\xa1seon Akrotir\xc3\xadou kai Dek\xc3\xa9lias</i>; <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Egemen \xc3\x9cs B\xc3\xb6lgeleri A\xc4\x9frotur ve Dikelya</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cyprus" title="Geography of Cyprus">island of Cyprus</a>. The areas, which include British military bases and installations, as well as other land, were retained by the British under the 1960 treaty of independence, signed by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> and representatives from the Greek and Turkish Cypriot communities, which granted independence to the <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a> of Cyprus. The territory serves an important role as a station for <a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence" title="Signals intelligence">signals intelligence</a> and provides a vital strategic part of the United Kingdom communications gathering and monitoring network in the Mediterranean and the Middle East.\n</p><p>The territory is composed of two Base Areas. One is Akrotiri (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">\xce\x91\xce\xba\xcf\x81\xcf\x89\xcf\x84\xce\xae\xcf\x81\xce\xb9</span> <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">[akro\xcb\x88tiri]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">A\xc4\x9frotur</i> <small>Turkish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Oghuz_languages" title="Help:IPA/Oghuz languages">[\xcb\x88\xc9\x91\xc9\xb0\xc9\xbeotu\xc9\xbe]</a></span>), or the <b>Western Sovereign Base Area</b> (<b>WSBA</b>), which includes two main bases at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Episkopi_Cantonment" title="Episkopi Cantonment">Episkopi</a>, plus all of <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_(village)" title="Akrotiri (village)">Akrotiri Village\'s district</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Limassol_Salt_Lake" title="Limassol Salt Lake">Limassol Salt Lake</a>) and parts of eleven other village districts.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The other area is <a href="/wiki/Dhekelia_Cantonment" title="Dhekelia Cantonment">Dhekelia Cantonment</a> (<span lang="el" title="Greek language text">\xce\x94\xce\xb5\xce\xba\xce\xad\xce\xbb\xce\xb5\xce\xb9\xce\xb1</span> <small>Greek pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">[\xc3\xb0e\xcb\x88ce\xca\x8ea]</a></span>; <i lang="tr" title="Turkish language text">Dikelya</i>), or the <b>Eastern Sovereign Base Area</b> (<b>ESBA</b>), which includes a base at <a href="/wiki/Ayios_Nikolaos_Station" title="Ayios Nikolaos Station">Ayios Nikolaos</a> plus parts of twelve village districts.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Criticism_and_disputes"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism and disputes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Reviews"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Reviews</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Governance"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Wildlife_and_ecology"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Wildlife and ecology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Transport_and_communications"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Transport and communications</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Travel_documents"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Travel documents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion,_Cyprus_(22440739916).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion%2C_Cyprus_%2822440739916%29.jpg/220px-The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion%2C_Cyprus_%2822440739916%29.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion%2C_Cyprus_%2822440739916%29.jpg/330px-The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion%2C_Cyprus_%2822440739916%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion%2C_Cyprus_%2822440739916%29.jpg/440px-The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion%2C_Cyprus_%2822440739916%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4806" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Sanctuary_and_Temple_of_Apollo_Hylates_at_Kourion,_Cyprus_(22440739916).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Remains of the sanctuary and temple of Apollo Hylates at <a href="/wiki/Kourion" title="Kourion">Kourion</a>, a UNESCO World Heritage Site</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg/220px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg/330px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg/440px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4832" data-file-height="2718" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Akrotiri_01-2017_img03_StNicholas_of_the_Cats.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_(village)#Holy_Monastery_of_St_Nicholas_of_the_Cats" title="Akrotiri (village)">Saint Nicholas of the Cats</a>, 2017</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cyprus_since_1878" title="History of Cyprus since 1878">History of Cyprus since 1878</a></div>\n<p>The Sovereign Base Areas were created in 1960 by the <a href="/wiki/London_and_Zurich_Agreements" class="mw-redirect" title="London and Zurich Agreements">London and Zurich Agreements</a>, when Cyprus achieved independence from the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. The United Kingdom desired to retain sovereignty over these areas, as this guaranteed the use of UK military bases on Cyprus, including <a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a>, and a garrison of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>. The importance of the bases to the British is based on the strategic location of the island, at the eastern edge of the Mediterranean, close to the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> and the Middle East; the ability to use the RAF base as staging post for military aircraft; and for training.\n</p><p>In July and August 1961, there was a series of bomb-attacks against the pipeline carrying fresh water to the Dhekelia Sovereign Base Area<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The pipeline was breached by explosions twelve times.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1974, following a military coup by the <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_National_Guard" title="Cypriot National Guard">Cypriot National Guard</a> attempting to achieve <i><a href="/wiki/Enosis" title="Enosis">enosis</a></i> (union with <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>), <a href="/wiki/Turkish_invasion_of_Cyprus" title="Turkish invasion of Cyprus">Turkey invaded the north of Cyprus</a>, leading to the establishment of the internationally unrecognised <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus">Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus</a>. This did not affect the status of the bases. <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriots" title="Greek Cypriots">Greek Cypriots</a> fleeing from the Turkish forces were permitted to travel through the Dhekelia Sovereign Base Area and were given humanitarian aid, with those from <a href="/wiki/Achna" title="Achna">Achna</a> setting up a new village (Dasaki Achnas or Achna Forest) which is still in the Dhekelia Sovereign Base Area.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The Turkish advance halted when it reached the edge of the Dhekelia Sovereign Base Area to avoid military conflict with the United Kingdom. In the Akrotiri Sovereign Base Area a tented refugee camp was set up at "Happy Valley" (part of the <a href="/wiki/Episkopi_Cantonment" title="Episkopi Cantonment">Episkopi Cantonment</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> to house Turkish Cypriots fleeing from Limassol and the villages surrounding the Area, until in 1975 they were flown out of RAF Akrotiri via Turkey to <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus" title="Northern Cyprus">northern Cyprus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Greek_Cypriot" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Cypriot">Greek Cypriot</a> refugees remain housed on land in the parts of <a href="/wiki/Trachoni" class="mw-redirect" title="Trachoni">Trachoni</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kolossi" title="Kolossi">Kolossi</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> villages that fall within the Akrotiri Sovereign Base Area.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_disputes">Criticism and disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Criticism and disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In July 2001, protests were held at the bases by local Cypriots, unhappy with British plans to construct <a href="/wiki/Radio_masts_and_towers" title="Radio masts and towers">radio masts</a> at the bases as part of an upgrade of British military communication posts around the world. Locals claimed the masts would endanger local lives and cause cancer, as well as have a negative impact on wildlife in the area. The British and Cypriot governments jointly commissioned health research from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bristol" title="University of Bristol">University of Bristol</a> and the Ministry of Health of the Republic of Cyprus, and that research project reported in 2005 that there was no evidence of health problems being caused by electromagnetic fields from the antennas.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The Sovereign Base Areas Administration has carried out assessments and surveys into the effects on wildlife, which have fed into an "Akrotiri Peninsula Environmental Management Plan", published in September 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The United Kingdom has shown no intention of ceding the Base Areas in their entirety to Cypriot control, although it has offered to cede 117 square kilometres (45&#160;sq&#160;mi) of farmland as part of the rejected <a href="/wiki/Annan_Plan_for_Cyprus" title="Annan Plan for Cyprus">Annan Plan for Cyprus</a>. As of  2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, around 3,000 troops of <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Cyprus" title="British Forces Cyprus">British Forces Cyprus</a> are based at Akrotiri and Dhekelia. <a href="/wiki/Ayios_Nikolaos_Station" title="Ayios Nikolaos Station">Ayios Nikolaos Station</a>, in the ESBA, is an <a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence#ELINT" title="Signals intelligence">ELINT</a> (electronic intelligence) listening station of the <a href="/wiki/UKUSA_Agreement" title="UKUSA Agreement">UKUSA Agreement</a> intelligence network.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The election of left-wing <a href="/wiki/Demetris_Christofias" title="Demetris Christofias">Demetris Christofias</a> as Cypriot president in February 2008 prompted concern in the United Kingdom. Christofias pledged to remove all foreign military forces from the island as part of a future settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_dispute" title="Cyprus dispute">Cyprus dispute</a>, calling the British presence on the island a "colonial bloodstain".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 29 August 2013, during the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_civil_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian civil war">Syrian civil war</a>, some Cypriot and British media sources speculated that long-range ballistic missiles, fired from Syria in retaliation for proposed British involvement in military intervention against the Syrian government of <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a>, could hit Cyprus, and could potentially deliver chemical weapons. In some Cypriot media it was stated that the proposed interdiction of the Syrian civil war, utilising Akrotiri and Dhekelia, could recklessly endanger the Cypriot populations near to those bases.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Two days earlier, on 27 August 2013, Cypriot foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Ioannis_Kasoulides" class="mw-redirect" title="Ioannis Kasoulides">Ioannis Kasoulides</a> had moved to calm Cypriot concerns, saying that the British bases were unlikely to play a major part in any intervention.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reviews">Reviews</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reviews">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In January 2010, a newspaper article appeared in the British press<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> claiming that as a result of budgetary constraints arising from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">British Ministry of Defence</a> drew up controversial<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> plans to withdraw the United Kingdom\'s 3,000 strong garrison and end the use of Cyprus as a staging point for ground forces. The Labour government under whom the proposal appeared was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Cameron%E2%80%93Clegg_coalition" title="Cameron\xe2\x80\x93Clegg coalition">Cameron\xe2\x80\x93Clegg coalition</a> and their defence review did not mention the issue.\n</p><p>On 15 December 2012 in a written statement to the lower house the Secretary of State for Defence of the UK government (<a href="/wiki/Philip_Hammond" title="Philip Hammond">Philip Hammond</a>) revealed the findings of a report on the SBA military bases following the completion of a review of their operations by Lord Ashcroft:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Sovereign Base areas are in a region of geo-political importance and high priority for the United Kingdom\xe2\x80\x99s long term national security interests ... Our military personnel, United Kingdom civilians and locally employed personnel in the Sovereign Base Areas make a major contribution to the national security of the United Kingdom and will continue to do so in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance <span id="Constitution_and_governance"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg/220px-USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg/330px-USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg/440px-USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC_CH-53_Akrotiri.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a> <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_CH-53_Sea_Stallion" title="Sikorsky CH-53 Sea Stallion">Sikorsky CH-53 Sea Stallion</a> at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG/220px-Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG/330px-Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG/440px-Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4327" data-file-height="3193" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Souvereign_Base_Areas_Police_station_on_Cyprus.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A SBA Police station in Akrotiri</div></div></div>\n<p>The SBAs were retained in 1960 to keep military bases in areas under British sovereignty, along with the rights retained to use other sites in what became the territory of the Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> That makes them different from the other remaining <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territories</a>, except for the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> which was similarly carved out of a former colony as a site for a military base, although in that case the base was to be used by the United States and the inhabitants (<a href="/wiki/Chagossians" title="Chagossians">Chagossians</a>) were all removed.\n</p><p>The basic philosophy of their administration was declared by the British government in Appendix O to the 1960 treaty with Cyprus, which provided that the British government intended:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Not to develop the Sovereign Base Areas for other than military purposes.</li>\n<li>Not to set up and administer "colonies".</li>\n<li>Not to create customs posts or other frontier barriers between the Sovereign Base Areas and the Republic.</li>\n<li>Not to set up or permit the establishment of civilian commercial or industrial enterprises except insofar as these are connected with military requirements, and not otherwise to impair the economic, commercial or industrial unity and life of the Island.</li>\n<li>Not to establish commercial or civilian seaports or airports.</li>\n<li>Not to allow new settlement of people in the Sovereign Base Areas other than for temporary purposes.</li>\n<li>Not to expropriate private property within the Sovereign Base Areas except for military purposes on payment of fair compensation.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>Appendix O also provides that various ancient monuments in the SBAs (in particular the site and remains of <a href="/wiki/Kourion" title="Kourion">Kourion</a>, the Sanctuary of Apollo <a href="/wiki/Hylates" title="Hylates">Hylates</a> near Kourion, the Stadium of Curium and the Church and remains of the <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_(village)#Holy_Monastery_of_St_Nicholas_of_the_Cats" title="Akrotiri (village)">Holy Monastery of St Nicholas of the Cats</a>) should be administered by the Republic of Cyprus. The Cypriot government issues licences for antiquity excavation in the SBAs subject to British consent, and any movable antiquities found in excavations or otherwise discovered become Cypriot state property.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nAccording to the British Ministry of Defence:</p><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Because the SBAs are primarily required as military bases and not ordinary dependent territories, the Administration reports to the Ministry of Defence in London. It has no formal connection with the Foreign and Commonwealth Office or the British High Commission in Nicosia, although there are close informal links with both offices on policy matters.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>The territory is administered by an Administrator who is also the Commander of British Forces Cyprus, which as of  February&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> has been <a href="/wiki/James_Illingworth" title="James Illingworth">Major-General James Illingworth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The Administrator is officially appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">British monarch</a> on the advice of the Ministry of Defence. The Administrator has all the executive and legislative authority of a governor of an overseas territory. A Chief Officer is appointed, and is responsible to the Administrator for the day-to-day running of the civil government, with subordinate Area Officers responsible for the civil administration of the two areas. No elections are held in the territory, although British citizens are normally entitled to vote in United Kingdom elections (as British Forces or overseas electors).\n</p><p>The areas have their own legal system, distinct from the United Kingdom and the Republic of Cyprus. This consists of the laws of the Colony of Cyprus as of August 1960, amended as necessary. The laws of Akrotiri and Dhekelia are closely aligned with, and in some cases identical to, the laws operating within the Republic of Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The Court of the Sovereign Base Areas is concerned with non-military offences committed by any person within Akrotiri and Dhekelia, and law and order is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Base_Areas_Police" title="Sovereign Base Areas Police">Sovereign Base Areas Police</a>, while offences involving British Forces Cyprus and military law are dealt with by the <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_Joint_Police_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyprus Joint Police Unit">Cyprus Joint Police Unit</a>. Fire and Rescue services are provided by the Defence Fire and Risk Management Organisation through stations at Episkopi, Akrotiri, Dhekelia and Ayios Nikolayos. The Defence Medical Services provide emergency ambulance cover based from medical centres in the main bases. All emergency services are accessible from any telephone using the Europe-wide emergency number 112.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA-Akrotiri.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CIA-Akrotiri.png/240px-CIA-Akrotiri.png" width="240" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/CIA-Akrotiri.png 1.5x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="353" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA-Akrotiri.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Akrotiri, Western Sovereign Base Area, <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Post_Office" title="British Forces Post Office">BFPO</a> 57.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA-Dhekelia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/CIA-Dhekelia.png/240px-CIA-Dhekelia.png" width="240" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/CIA-Dhekelia.png 1.5x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="353" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA-Dhekelia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Dhekelia, Eastern Sovereign Base Area, <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Post_Office" title="British Forces Post Office">BFPOs</a> 58 &amp; 59.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cyprus" title="Geography of Cyprus">Geography of Cyprus</a></div>\n<p>Akrotiri and Dhekelia cover 3% of the land area of Cyprus, a total of 254&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (98&#160;sq&#160;mi) (split 123&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (47&#160;sq&#160;mi) (48.5%) at Akrotiri and 131&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (51&#160;sq&#160;mi) (51.5%) at Dhekelia). 60% of the land is privately owned as freeholds by Cypriot citizens; the other 40% is controlled by the Ministry of Defence as <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">the Crown</a> leasehold land.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In January 2014, an agreement between the Cypriot and UK governments was signed, ensuring that residents and property owners in the British Bases will enjoy equal rights for the development of property.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In addition to Akrotiri and Dhekelia, the Treaty of Establishment also provided for the continued use by the British Ministry of Defence and the British Armed Forces of certain facilities within the Republic of Cyprus, known as <i>Retained Sites</i>.\n</p><p>Akrotiri is located in the south of the island, near the city of <a href="/wiki/Limassol" title="Limassol">Limassol</a> (or Lemesos). Dhekelia is in the southeast, near <a href="/wiki/Larnaca" title="Larnaca">Larnaca</a>. Both areas include military bases, as well as farmland and some residential land. Akrotiri is surrounded by territory controlled by the Republic of Cyprus, but Dhekelia also borders on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Buffer_Zone_in_Cyprus" title="United Nations Buffer Zone in Cyprus">United Nations (UN) buffer zone</a> and the area controlled by the Turkish forces.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ayia_Napa" title="Ayia Napa">Ayia Napa</a> lies to the east of Dhekelia. The villages of <a href="/wiki/Xylotympou" class="mw-redirect" title="Xylotympou">Xylotympou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ormideia" title="Ormideia">Ormideia</a>, also in the Republic of Cyprus, are enclaves surrounded by Dhekelia. The <a href="/wiki/Dhekelia_Power_Station" title="Dhekelia Power Station">Dhekelia Power Station</a>, divided by a British road into two parts, also belongs to the Republic of Cyprus. The northern part is an enclave, like the two villages, whereas the southern part is located by the sea, and therefore not an enclave, though it has no territorial waters of its own.\n</p><p>Territorial waters of 3 nautical miles (5.556&#160;km) are claimed, and the right <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_the_Law_of_the_Sea" title="United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea">according to the laws of the UN</a> to extend the claim of up to 12 nautical miles (22.224&#160;km) is reserved.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg/240px-20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg" width="240" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg/360px-20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg/480px-20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20061019_Episkopi_Bay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Episkopi Bay is on the west coast of Akrotiri.</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_and_ecology">Wildlife and ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Wildlife and ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Cyprus is an important <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">migration flyway</a> for birds between Africa and Europe and <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration_perils" title="Bird migration perils">millions of birds are killed yearly</a> as they migrate over the island. To protect resident and migratory birds, <a href="/wiki/BirdLife_Cyprus" title="BirdLife Cyprus">BirdLife Cyprus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_for_the_Protection_of_Birds" title="Royal Society for the Protection of Birds">RSPB</a> survey areas of illegal trapping. More than 150 species of birds, over half of conservation concern, have been trapped in nets, or on <a href="/wiki/Birdlime" title="Birdlime">limesticks</a>, and it is estimated that organised crime gangs earn over 15 million Euros yearly. The dead birds are sold to provide the main ingredient for <a href="/wiki/Ambelopoulia" title="Ambelopoulia">ambelopoulia</a> in the Republic of Cyprus; an illegal delicacy served to restaurant diners. The 2015 survey estimated a maximum 19&#160;km (12&#160;mi) of mist nets across both the Republic and the British Territories, and more than 5,300 limesticks removed, mainly in the Republic. It is estimated that over 2 million birds were killed in 2015 including over 800,000 on British Territories.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Employing measures such as covert camera surveillance (including a drone), exclusion zones and impounding vehicles, trapping activity at Dhekelia fell by 72%. In 2016 an estimated 800,000 birds were killed at Dhekelia and in the following year trapping activity fell by 72% and bird deaths to an estimated 180,000.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The beaches in the British Sovereign Base Areas (SBAs) are important nesting sites for the endangered green <i>Chelonia mydas</i> and loggerhead <i>Caretta caretta</i> turtles. The SBA Environment Department, assisted by a large volunteer effort, has monitored turtle nesting success on SBA beaches since 1990. Disturbance to nesting turtles is an issue in some areas due to activities such as camping, driving on beaches and illegal fishing. Sea turtles in Cyprus are protected as priority species under the Protection and Management of Nature and Wildlife Ordinance (implementing the provisions of the Habitats Directive), enacted in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2015, five <a href="/wiki/Special_Areas_of_Conservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Areas of Conservation">Special Areas of Conservation</a> (SACs) were designated in the Cyprus Sovereign Base Areas. The five SACs designated are Akrotiri, Episkopi, Cape Pyla, Dhekelia and Agios Nikolaos.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The designations were made under the Protection and Management of Nature and Wildlife Ordinance and will support the existing network (<a href="/wiki/Natura_2000" title="Natura 2000">NATURA 2000</a>) of SACs in Cyprus and across Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Cyprus" title="Languages of Cyprus">Languages of Cyprus</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg/220px-Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg/330px-Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg/440px-Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3312" data-file-height="4416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britse_telefooncel_op_Cyprus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A British <a href="/wiki/Red_telephone_box" title="Red telephone box">red telephone box</a> in Dhekelia</div></div></div>\n<p>When the areas were being established, the boundaries were deliberately drawn to avoid centres of population. Approximately 15,700 people live in the areas. About 7,700 native Cypriots work in the areas themselves, or on farmland within the boundaries of the areas. The British military and their families make up the rest of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Persons related to the territory may in theory be eligible to claim the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories_citizen" title="British Overseas Territories citizen">British Overseas Territories citizenship</a> (BOTC status) through a personal connection to the areas (i.e., birth on the territory before 1983, or born after 1983 to a parent who were born on the territory before 1983); but unlike most other British Overseas Territories, there is no provision in the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories_Act_2002" title="British Overseas Territories Act 2002">2002 amendment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Nationality_Act_1981" title="British Nationality Act 1981">British Nationality Act 1981</a> by which British citizenship (with the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_abode_(United_Kingdom)" title="Right of abode (United Kingdom)">right of abode in the United Kingdom</a>) can either be claimed through automatic entitlement or be applied for by means of registration, from or through a sole personal connection to the Base Areas. (In comparison, the 2002 act bestowed British citizenship on all other BOTCs.) Hence non-British and non-military personnel with the connection to the territory can only live and work in the UK through their EU (Cypriot) citizenship and not through their BOTC status.\n</p><p>Under the terms of the 1960 agreement with Cyprus establishing the Sovereign Base Areas, the United Kingdom is committed not to use the areas for civilian purposes. This was stated in 2002 as the primary reason for the exclusion of the areas from the scope of the <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories_Act_2002" title="British Overseas Territories Act 2002">British Overseas Territories Act 2002</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg/220px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg/330px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg/440px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5034" data-file-height="2832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Akrotiri_01-2017_img11_Akrotiri_village.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Akrotiri village</div></div></div>\n<p>There are no economic statistics gathered for Akrotiri and Dhekelia. The main economic activities are the provision of services to the military, as well as limited agriculture. When the territory under the effective control of the Republic of Cyprus switched currencies from the <a href="/wiki/Cypriot_pound" title="Cypriot pound">Cypriot pound</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> on 1 January 2008, Akrotiri and Dhekelia followed suit making the Sovereign Base Areas the only territory under British sovereignty to officially use the euro.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg/220px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg/330px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg/440px-Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4289" data-file-height="2412" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Akrotiri_01-2017_img01_BBC_transmitter_masts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a> transmitter masts in Akrotiri</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service#BFBS_Radio" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">BFBS Radio 1 and 2</a> are broadcast on <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM</a> and can be widely received across Cyprus. <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service#BFBS_Television" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">BFBS Television</a> is now only available to entitled viewers via satellite, having been confined to the SBAs or encrypted in 1997 for copyright reasons,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> before BFBS switched off its analogue transmitters in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/British_East_Mediterranean_Relay_Station" title="British East Mediterranean Relay Station">British East Mediterranean Relay Station</a> is situated locally.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_and_communications">Transport and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Transport and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Cypriot motorways pass through both areas. There is no public airport within the areas, but the <a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a> airbase is located there, which has a runway suitable for long distance flights, but not used for public flights.\n</p><p>The Base Areas form part of the Republic of Cyprus <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">telephone numbering plan</a>, using the international prefix <a href="/wiki/%2B357" class="mw-redirect" title="+357">+357</a>. Landline numbers are in the same eight-digit format, with the last four digits being the extension number. Numbers in Dhekelia begin with the digits <b>2474</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> while those in Akrotiri begin with the digits <b>2527</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Postal services are provided by the <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Post_Office" title="British Forces Post Office">British Forces Post Office</a>, with mail to Akrotiri being addressed to <b>BFPO 57</b><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and mail to Dhekelia and Ayios Nikolaos being addressed to <b>BFPO 58</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The bases are issued different <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">amateur radio</a> <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio_callsigns_of_the_Middle_East#Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Amateur radio callsigns of the Middle East">call signs</a> from the Republic of Cyprus. Amateur radio stations on the bases use the <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a> prefix of "ZC4", which is assigned to Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> There are about 52 amateurs licensed in this manner.\n</p><p>Amateur <a href="/wiki/Radio_Direction_Finding" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Direction Finding">radio direction finding</a> identified RAF Akrotiri as the location of the powerful but now defunct <a href="/wiki/Shortwave_radio" title="Shortwave radio">shortwave</a> <a href="/wiki/Numbers_station" title="Numbers station">numbers station</a> "<a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Poacher_(numbers_station)" title="Lincolnshire Poacher (numbers station)">Lincolnshire Poacher</a>". Several <a href="/wiki/HRS_antenna" class="mw-redirect" title="HRS antenna">curtain antennas</a> there have been identified as being used for these transmissions.<sup id="cite_ref-Numbers_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Numbers-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Service_Children%27s_Education" title="Service Children&#39;s Education">Service Children\'s Education</a> oversees education for children of personnel and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">MoD</a> employees. The Eastern Sovereign Base Area is served by Dhekelia Primary School and Ayios Nikolaos Primary School, which are feeders for <a href="/wiki/King_Richard_School,_Cyprus" title="King Richard School, Cyprus">King Richard School</a>. The Western Sovereign Base Area is served by Episkopi Primary School and Akrotiri Primary School, which are feeders for <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_School,_Cyprus" title="St. John&#39;s School, Cyprus">St. John\'s School</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Travel_documents">Travel documents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Travel documents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Borders of Akrotiri and Dhekelia">Borders of Akrotiri and Dhekelia</a></div>\n<p>There is normally no passport check at the border from Akrotiri or Dhekelia to Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Possession of a passport, or a <a href="/wiki/National_identity_cards_in_the_European_Economic_Area" title="National identity cards in the European Economic Area">EU compliant national identity card</a> is generally needed in Cyprus.\n</p><p>A passport is required to travel between <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>/SBAs and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus" title="Northern Cyprus">Northern Cyprus</a>. Issues concerning the validity of car insurance and customs are specified by SBAs\' administration.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation"
